## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# Team Handoff: Envoy ext_authz Filter

You are taking over ownership of the **ext_authz HTTP filter** from a departing team member. Your task is to produce a comprehensive handoff document that will help you (and future maintainers) understand this component.

## Context

The ext_authz filter is one of Envoy's authorization extensions. Your predecessor maintained it for the past year but is moving to a different project. You need to quickly build a working mental model of this component.

## Your Task

Explore the Envoy codebase and produce a handoff document at `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` covering the following sections:

### 1. Purpose
What does the ext_authz filter do? What problems does it solve? When would someone use it?

### 2. Dependencies
- **Upstream dependencies**: What other Envoy components or libraries does ext_authz depend on?
- **Downstream consumers**: What uses or integrates with ext_authz? How is it configured in Envoy's filter chain?

### 3. Relevant Components
List the most important source files for this filter. For each file, explain its role (e.g., "configuration parsing", "request handling", "gRPC client implementation").

### 4. Failure Modes
What can go wrong? What are common failure scenarios? How does the filter handle errors (e.g., authorization service unavailable, timeout, network failure)?

### 5. Testing
How is this filter tested? Where are the tests located? Are there integration tests, unit tests, or both?

### 6. Debugging
If something goes wrong with ext_authz in production, how would you debug it? What logs, metrics, or traces would you look at?

## Deliverable

Write your findings to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md` using the following structure:

```
# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document

## 1. Purpose
[Your findings here]

## 2. Dependencies
### Upstream Dependencies
[What ext_authz depends on]

### Downstream Consumers
[What depends on ext_authz]

## 3. Relevant Components
- **path/to/file.cc**: [Role/responsibility]
- **path/to/file.h**: [Role/responsibility]
...

## 4. Failure Modes
[Failure scenarios and error handling]

## 5. Testing
[Test locations, test types, how to run tests]

## 6. Debugging
[Debugging strategies, observability]
```

## Guidelines

- Be specific. Reference actual file paths, class names, function names.
- Focus on understanding the **system's behavior**, not just describing the code.
- This is analysis only — do not modify any code.
- Use code search and file exploration tools to explore the codebase efficiently.

66-assistanttext-
The handoff document has been written to `/logs/agent/onboarding.md`. Here's a summary of what it covers:

**Section 1 - Purpose**: The ext_authz filter delegates HTTP authorization to an external service via gRPC or HTTP, supporting centralized policy engines like OPA.

**Section 2 - Dependencies**: Maps all upstream dependencies (common ext_authz library, gRPC/HTTP client implementations, check request utilities, mutation rules, proto definitions) and downstream consumers (HTTP connection manager filter chain, per-route config, access logging via FilterState, dynamic metadata for downstream filters).

**Section 3 - Relevant Components**: Lists all 15+ source files with their specific roles — from the main filter (`ext_authz.h/.cc`), config factory (`config.h/.cc`), common client interface (`ext_authz.h`), gRPC implementation (`ext_authz_grpc_impl.*`), HTTP implementation (`ext_authz_http_impl.*`), check request builder (`check_request_utils.*`), to proto definitions.

**Section 4 - Failure Modes**: Covers 7 failure scenarios — service unavailable, fail-open vs fail-closed behavior, authorization denied, invalid response mutations, request body too large, filter disabled, timeouts, and header limit violations. Each includes the specific code path and counter incremented.

**Section 5 - Testing**: Documents unit tests, integration tests, fuzz tests, and test support files across 14+ test files, with Bazel commands to run them.

**Section 6 - Debugging**: Covers log levels and key messages, 11 stats counters with meanings, tracing span tags, FilterState fields for access logging, response flags (`UF`), response code details, dynamic metadata, and a step-by-step debugging workflow.

27. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document\n\n## 1. Purpose\n\nThe ext_authz HTTP filter (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) implements external authorization for Envoy proxy. It delegates authorization decisions to an external service before allowing requests to proceed upstream.\n\n**What it does:**\n\n- Intercepts incoming HTTP requests and constructs an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) containing request attributes (headers, path, method, source/destination info, TLS details, request body, metadata).\n- Sends this check request to a configured external authorization service via either **gRPC** (using the `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` RPC) or **raw HTTP** (by forwarding selected headers to an HTTP cluster).\n- Based on the response (`OK`, `Denied`, or `Error`), the filter either allows the request to continue upstream (potentially mutating headers/query parameters), returns a denial response to the client, or handles the error according to its `failure_mode_allow` configuration.\n\n**When to use it:**\n\n- When authorization logic needs to live outside Envoy (e.g., a centralized policy engine like OPA, a custom auth service, or a third-party authorization provider).\n- When you need to enforce access control policies that require context beyond what Envoy natively evaluates (e.g., checking JWTs against a user database, enforcing RBAC policies, rate limiting based on user identity).\n- When different routes/virtual hosts need different authorization behavior (via per-route configuration).\n\nThere is also a **network-level** variant (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`) at `source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/` that operates at the TCP layer, but this document focuses on the HTTP filter.\n\n## 2. Dependencies\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe ext_authz HTTP filter depends on the following Envoy components and libraries:\n\n| Dependency | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`** | Core `Client` interface, `Response` struct, `CheckStatus` enum, `RequestCallbacks` interface. This is the abstract interface both gRPC and HTTP client implementations satisfy. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.{h,cc}`** | `GrpcClientImpl` \u2014 gRPC client that sends `CheckRequest` to `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` using Envoy's async gRPC client. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.{h,cc}`** | `RawHttpClientImpl` \u2014 HTTP client that sends authorization checks as raw HTTP requests to a configured cluster. Also contains `ClientConfig` for HTTP-specific configuration (header matchers, path prefix, retry policy, tracing). |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.{h,cc}`** | `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()` \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` protobuf from HTTP stream attributes (headers, body, peer info, TLS, metadata). Also provides `Matcher` classes for header key matching. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.{h,cc}`** | `MutationRules::Checker` \u2014 validates header mutations from the authz response against configured rules (e.g., disallowing modification of certain headers). |\n| **`envoy/http/filter.h`** | `Http::StreamFilter` interface that the filter implements (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`, `encodeHeaders`, etc.). |\n| **`envoy/grpc/async_client_manager.h`** | Used to create/retrieve gRPC async clients for communicating with the authorization service. |\n| **`envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`** | Used by the HTTP client to find the thread-local cluster for the authorization service. |\n| **`envoy/runtime/runtime.h`** | Runtime feature flags for `filter_enabled` (fractional percentage) and `deny_at_disable`. |\n| **`envoy/stats/scope.h`, `envoy/stats/stats_macros.h`** | Stats infrastructure for counters (`ok`, `denied`, `error`, `disabled`, `failure_mode_allowed`, `invalid`, etc.). |\n| **`envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h`** | `FilterState` used to store `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` for access logging and CEL. |\n| **`source/common/http/utility.h`** | HTTP utilities (query parameter parsing, WebSocket/H2 upgrade detection, per-filter-config resolution). |\n| **`source/common/router/config_impl.h`** | Route configuration utilities. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h`** | `FactoryBase` template used by `ExtAuthzFilterConfig` for filter registration. |\n\n**Proto dependencies:**\n\n- `envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.proto` \u2014 Filter configuration (`ExtAuthz`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `CheckSettings`, `HttpService`, `BufferSettings`).\n- `envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto` \u2014 The `CheckRequest`/`CheckResponse` messages and `Authorization` service definition.\n- `envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto` \u2014 gRPC service configuration.\n- `envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto` \u2014 Header mutation rules.\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Envoy HTTP Connection Manager**: The filter is instantiated as part of the HTTP filter chain. It is registered under the name `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` (legacy name: `envoy.ext_authz`) via `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY` in `config.cc:84`.\n- **Per-route configuration**: Virtual hosts, routes, and weighted clusters can customize behavior via `ExtAuthzPerRoute` (disable the filter, add context extensions, override the authorization service, override body buffering settings). The filter resolves per-route config via `Http::Utility::resolveMostSpecificPerFilterConfig<FilterConfigPerRoute>()` and merges configs from multiple levels.\n- **Access logging / CEL**: `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` is stored in `FilterState` under the filter's config name, exposing fields like `latency_us`, `bytesSent`, `bytesReceived` for use in access log formatters and CEL expressions.\n- **Dynamic metadata**: The filter writes dynamic metadata under namespace `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` that downstream filters can consume (e.g., the `ext_authz_duration` field).\n- **Network ext_authz filter**: `source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/` is a sibling TCP-level filter sharing the same common library (`filters/common/ext_authz/`).\n\n## 3. Relevant Components\n\n### Core HTTP Filter\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Main filter header. Defines:\n  - `ExtAuthzFilterStats` \u2014 counter definitions (`ok`, `denied`, `error`, `disabled`, `failure_mode_allowed`, `invalid`, `ignored_dynamic_metadata`, `filter_state_name_collision`, `omitted_response_headers`, `request_header_limits_reached`, `response_header_limits_reached`).\n  - `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` \u2014 `FilterState::Object` storing per-request latency, bytes sent/received, cluster info, upstream host, gRPC status for access logging.\n  - `FilterConfig` \u2014 immutable configuration parsed from proto (failure mode, body buffering, header mutation rules, status on error, metadata namespaces, etc.).\n  - `FilterConfigPerRoute` \u2014 per-route settings (context extensions, disable flag, body buffering override, per-route gRPC/HTTP service override).\n  - `Filter` \u2014 the `Http::StreamFilter` implementation with state machine (`NotStarted` -> `Calling` -> `Complete`).\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.cc`**: Main filter implementation. Key functions:\n  - `FilterConfig::FilterConfig()` (line 77) \u2014 parses proto configuration into C++ fields.\n  - `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (line 398) \u2014 entry point; checks per-route flags, decides whether to buffer body, initiates the check call.\n  - `Filter::decodeData()` (line 451) \u2014 handles request body buffering.\n  - `Filter::initiateCall()` (line 275) \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` via `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()`, merges per-route context extensions, handles per-route service overrides, and calls `client_->check()`.\n  - `Filter::onComplete()` (line 631) \u2014 callback handling the `CheckResponse`: OK path (mutates request headers, query params, saves response headers), Denied path (sends local reply with authz-specified status/headers/body), Error path (failure_mode_allow or reject).\n  - `Filter::onDestroy()` (line 613) \u2014 cancels in-flight requests.\n  - `Filter::encodeHeaders()` (line 489) \u2014 adds saved response headers to the upstream response on the encode path.\n  - `Filter::createPerRouteGrpcClient()` (line 208) \u2014 creates a gRPC client for per-route service overrides.\n  - `Filter::createPerRouteHttpClient()` (line 252) \u2014 creates an HTTP client for per-route service overrides.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.h`**: Filter factory (`ExtAuthzFilterConfig`). Registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.cc`**: Factory implementation. Creates either a `GrpcClientImpl` or `RawHttpClientImpl` based on configuration (line 31: `if (proto_config.has_http_service())`).\n\n### Common Library (shared with network ext_authz)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Abstract `Client` interface with `check()` and `cancel()` methods. `Response` struct with `CheckStatus` (`OK`, `Denied`, `Error`), header mutations, body, status code, dynamic metadata, gRPC status. `RequestCallbacks` with `onComplete()`. Tracing constants and response code details.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.h/.cc`**: `GrpcClientImpl` \u2014 sends unary gRPC `Check` RPC. Handles `onSuccess()` (parses `OkHttpResponse`/`DeniedHttpResponse`/`ErrorHttpResponse`, copies header mutations, dynamic metadata) and `onFailure()` (returns `CheckStatus::Error`).\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.h/.cc`**: `RawHttpClientImpl` \u2014 sends HTTP request to the authorization cluster. `ClientConfig` manages header matchers for upstream/client/dynamic-metadata headers. `toResponse()` maps HTTP 200 to OK, 5xx to Error, everything else to Denied. Supports retry policy.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.h/.cc`**: `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()` \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` proto from stream callbacks, headers, body, peer certificates, TLS session, metadata, destination labels, and header matchers.\n\n### Proto Definitions\n\n- **`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.proto`**: `ExtAuthz` message (main config), `HttpService`, `AuthorizationRequest`, `AuthorizationResponse`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `CheckSettings`, `BufferSettings`.\n- **`api/envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto`**: `CheckRequest`, `CheckResponse`, `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, `ErrorHttpResponse`, `Authorization` service with `Check` RPC.\n\n### Build Configuration\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/BUILD`**: Bazel build file listing all deps for the `ext_authz` library and `config` extension.\n\n## 4. Failure Modes\n\n### Authorization Service Unavailable\n\n- **gRPC**: `GrpcClientImpl::onFailure()` is called with a non-OK gRPC status. This produces a `Response` with `CheckStatus::Error` and the gRPC status code.\n- **HTTP**: If the cluster doesn't exist (`thread_local_cluster == nullptr`), `errorResponse()` is returned immediately. If the HTTP request fails (connection reset, buffer limit exceeded), `RawHttpClientImpl::onFailure()` returns `errorResponse()`. If the authz server returns HTTP 5xx, `toResponse()` treats it as an error.\n\n### Error Handling in the Filter (`onComplete` with `CheckStatus::Error`)\n\nThe `failure_mode_allow` configuration determines behavior (ext_authz.cc, line 1039):\n\n- **`failure_mode_allow: true`** (fail-open): The request is allowed through. The `failure_mode_allowed` counter is incremented. If `failure_mode_allow_header_add` is also true, the header `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed: true` is added to the request so upstream services know auth was skipped. A custom error response status code, headers, and body from the authorization server can also be used.\n- **`failure_mode_allow: false`** (fail-closed, the default): A local reply is sent with the configured `status_on_error` (default: HTTP 403 Forbidden) or a custom status code from the error response. The response flag `UnauthorizedExternalService` is set.\n\n### Authorization Denied\n\nWhen the authz service denies the request (ext_authz.cc, line 944):\n- The `denied` counter is incremented.\n- The response flag `UnauthorizedExternalService` is set.\n- A local reply is sent with the status code from the authz response (default: HTTP 403), the response body (optionally truncated to `max_denied_response_body_bytes`), and headers specified by the authz server.\n\n### Invalid Authorization Response\n\nWhen `validate_mutations: true` and the authz response contains invalid headers or query parameters (ext_authz.cc, line 1091):\n- The `invalid` counter is incremented.\n- A local reply with HTTP 500 is sent with response code detail `ext_authz_invalid`.\n\n### Request Body Too Large\n\nWhen `with_request_body.max_request_bytes` is set and `allow_partial_message: false`:\n- If the body exceeds the limit, Envoy returns HTTP 413 (Payload Too Large) *without* calling the authz service.\n- If `allow_partial_message: true`, the body is truncated and sent with the `x-envoy-auth-partial-body: true` header.\n\n### Filter Disabled\n\nWhen the filter is disabled (via runtime flag or per-route config):\n- If `deny_at_disable` is true, requests are rejected with `status_on_error`.\n- Otherwise, requests pass through without authorization.\n\n### Timeout\n\n- Both gRPC and HTTP clients support configurable timeouts (default: 200ms).\n- A timeout results in an error response, handled the same as service unavailability.\n\n### Header/Response Limits\n\n- `enforce_response_header_limits: true` causes the filter to send HTTP 500 if adding response headers from the authz service would exceed the header map's size or count limits.\n- `request_header_limits_reached` and `response_header_limits_reached` counters track these events.\n\n## 5. Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc`**: Comprehensive unit tests for the HTTP filter. Tests cover all response paths (OK, Denied, Error), header mutation, body buffering, per-route configuration, dynamic metadata, failure modes, query parameter mutations, header validation, and edge cases. Uses mocked `Client` and `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks`.\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config_test.cc`**: Tests for the filter factory configuration parsing.\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl_test.cc`**: Unit tests for the gRPC client implementation (response parsing, header copying, error handling, dynamic metadata).\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl_test.cc`**: Unit tests for the HTTP client implementation (request construction, response parsing, header matching, error handling, retry policy).\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils_test.cc`**: Tests for `CheckRequest` construction from stream attributes.\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc`**: End-to-end integration tests using Envoy's integration test framework. Tests gRPC and HTTP authz services, body buffering, header manipulation, per-route overrides, and failure modes. Includes tests with both HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 downstream protocols.\n\n### Fuzz Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_fuzz_test.cc`**: Fuzz testing for gRPC ext_authz.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_fuzz_test.cc`**: Fuzz testing for HTTP ext_authz.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz_lib.{h,cc}`**: Shared fuzz test library.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz.proto`**: Proto for fuzz test cases.\n- Fuzz corpus directories: `ext_authz_grpc_corpus/`, `ext_authz_http_corpus/`.\n\n### Test Support Files\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/mocks.{h,cc}`**: Mock `Client` implementation for unit testing.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/test_common.{h,cc}`**: Test utilities (e.g., `TestCommon::makeCheckResponse()`).\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/logging_test_filter.{cc,proto}`**: A test filter used in integration tests to verify logging info in filter state.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.yaml`**: Example YAML configuration for tests.\n\n### Running Tests\n\nTests are built using Bazel. To run specific tests:\n\n```bash\n# Unit tests for the HTTP filter\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_test\n\n# Integration tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_integration_test\n\n# Common library tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:ext_authz_grpc_impl_test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:ext_authz_http_impl_test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:check_request_utils_test\n```\n\n## 6. Debugging\n\n### Logs\n\nThe filter uses Envoy's logging framework with logger ID `ext_authz`:\n\n- **Trace level** (`-l trace`): Most detailed. Logs every header mutation, check request/response details, query parameter changes, body buffering decisions.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter calling authorization server.\"` \u2014 Check call initiated.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter added header(s) to the request:\"` \u2014 Header mutations on OK response.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter rejected the request. Response status code: '{}'\"` \u2014 Denied response.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter allowed the request with error\"` \u2014 Failure mode allowed.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter is buffering the request\"` \u2014 Body buffering active.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter is truncating the response body from {} to {} bytes.\"` \u2014 Body truncation.\n\n- **Debug level**: Key decision points like buffering start/stop, route cache clearing, per-route client creation.\n  - `\"ext_authz is clearing route cache\"` \u2014 Route cache cleared after header mutation.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter: using per-route gRPC service configuration.\"` \u2014 Per-route override active.\n  - `\"ext_authz cluster '{}' does not exist\"` \u2014 HTTP client cluster missing.\n\n- **Warn level**: Used with `ENVOY_LOG_EVERY_POW_2` for response header limit violations and per-route client creation failures.\n\n- The gRPC client logs at trace level: `\"Sending CheckRequest: {}\"` and `\"Received CheckResponse: {}\"` with full proto debug strings.\n\n### Stats / Metrics\n\nAll counters are prefixed with `ext_authz.` (or `ext_authz.<stat_prefix>.` if `stat_prefix` is configured):\n\n| Counter | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ext_authz.ok` | Requests authorized successfully |\n| `ext_authz.denied` | Requests denied by the authz service |\n| `ext_authz.error` | Errors communicating with the authz service |\n| `ext_authz.disabled` | Requests where the filter was disabled (via runtime or metadata) |\n| `ext_authz.failure_mode_allowed` | Requests allowed through despite authz errors (fail-open) |\n| `ext_authz.invalid` | Responses rejected due to invalid mutations (`validate_mutations: true`) |\n| `ext_authz.ignored_dynamic_metadata` | Dynamic metadata rejected because ingestion is disabled |\n| `ext_authz.filter_state_name_collision` | Filter state name already in use by another filter |\n| `ext_authz.omitted_response_headers` | Response headers dropped due to header map limits |\n| `ext_authz.request_header_limits_reached` | Request header mutations rejected due to limits |\n| `ext_authz.response_header_limits_reached` | Response header mutations rejected due to limits |\n\nAdditionally, if `charge_cluster_response_stats: true` (default), the filter increments cluster-scoped stats (e.g., `cluster.<cluster>.ext_authz.ok`, `cluster.<cluster>.ext_authz.denied`, etc.) and charges HTTP response code stats against the cluster for denied responses.\n\n### Traces\n\n- The gRPC client creates a child span from the parent span passed to `check()`. The span is tagged with:\n  - `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok`, `ext_authz_unauthorized`, or `ext_authz_error`.\n- The HTTP client creates a child span named `\"async <cluster> egress\"`. The span is tagged with:\n  - `ext_authz_http_status`: The HTTP status code from the authz server.\n  - `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok` or `ext_authz_unauthorized`.\n\n### Filter State (Access Logging)\n\nWhen `emit_filter_state_stats: true`, the filter writes `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` to `FilterState` under the filter's config name. This exposes:\n\n- `latency_us` \u2014 Authorization call latency in microseconds (available for both gRPC and HTTP).\n- `bytesSent` \u2014 Bytes sent to the authz service (gRPC only).\n- `bytesReceived` \u2014 Bytes received from the authz service (gRPC only).\n- Upstream host and cluster info (gRPC only).\n- gRPC status code (gRPC only).\n\nThese can be referenced in access log format strings and CEL expressions.\n\n### Response Flags\n\nThe filter sets the `UF` (UnauthorizedExternalService) response flag on denied and error (fail-closed) responses. This appears in access logs as `UF`.\n\n### Response Code Details\n\nThe filter sets response code details that appear in access logs:\n\n- `ext_authz_denied` \u2014 Request was denied.\n- `ext_authz_error` \u2014 Authz service error (fail-closed).\n- `ext_authz_invalid` \u2014 Invalid authz response was rejected.\n\n### Dynamic Metadata\n\nOn OK responses, the filter writes dynamic metadata under `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` including the authz service's dynamic metadata and `ext_authz_duration` (latency in milliseconds). This can be logged or used by downstream filters.\n\n### Common Debugging Workflow\n\n1. **Check stats**: Look at `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error` counters to understand the distribution of responses.\n2. **Enable trace logging**: Set log level to `trace` for the `ext_authz` logger to see full request/response details.\n3. **Check response flags**: Look for `UF` in access logs to identify authz-related failures.\n4. **Check response code details**: `ext_authz_denied`, `ext_authz_error`, or `ext_authz_invalid` indicate the specific failure type.\n5. **Verify cluster health**: Ensure the authz service cluster is healthy (check `cluster.<cluster>.membership_healthy`, `cluster.<cluster>.upstream_rq_*` stats).\n6. **Check timeouts**: If `ext_authz.error` is high, check if the authz service is responding within the configured timeout (default: 200ms).\n7. **Inspect tracing**: Use distributed tracing to see the ext_authz child span, its duration, and status tags.\n8. **Filter state stats**: If `emit_filter_state_stats` is enabled, check access logs for latency and bytes metrics per request.\n",

  "content": "# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document\n\n## 1. Purpose\n\nThe ext_authz HTTP filter (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) implements external authorization for Envoy proxy. It delegates authorization decisions to an external service before allowing requests to proceed upstream.\n\n**What it does:**\n\n- Intercepts incoming HTTP requests and constructs an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) containing request attributes (headers, path, method, source/destination info, TLS details, request body, metadata).\n- Sends this check request to a configured external authorization service via either **gRPC** (using the `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` RPC) or **raw HTTP** (by forwarding selected headers to an HTTP cluster).\n- Based on the response (`OK`, `Denied`, or `Error`), the filter either allows the request to continue upstream (potentially mutating headers/query parameters), returns a denial response to the client, or handles the error according to its `failure_mode_allow` configuration.\n\n**When to use it:**\n\n- When authorization logic needs to live outside Envoy (e.g., a centralized policy engine like OPA, a custom auth service, or a third-party authorization provider).\n- When you need to enforce access control policies that require context beyond what Envoy natively evaluates (e.g., checking JWTs against a user database, enforcing RBAC policies, rate limiting based on user identity).\n- When different routes/virtual hosts need different authorization behavior (via per-route configuration).\n\nThere is also a **network-level** variant (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`) at `source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/` that operates at the TCP layer, but this document focuses on the HTTP filter.\n\n## 2. Dependencies\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe ext_authz HTTP filter depends on the following Envoy components and libraries:\n\n| Dependency | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`** | Core `Client` interface, `Response` struct, `CheckStatus` enum, `RequestCallbacks` interface. This is the abstract interface both gRPC and HTTP client implementations satisfy. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.{h,cc}`** | `GrpcClientImpl` \u2014 gRPC client that sends `CheckRequest` to `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` using Envoy's async gRPC client. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.{h,cc}`** | `RawHttpClientImpl` \u2014 HTTP client that sends authorization checks as raw HTTP requests to a configured cluster. Also contains `ClientConfig` for HTTP-specific configuration (header matchers, path prefix, retry policy, tracing). |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.{h,cc}`** | `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()` \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` protobuf from HTTP stream attributes (headers, body, peer info, TLS, metadata). Also provides `Matcher` classes for header key matching. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/common/mutation_rules/mutation_rules.{h,cc}`** | `MutationRules::Checker` \u2014 validates header mutations from the authz response against configured rules (e.g., disallowing modification of certain headers). |\n| **`envoy/http/filter.h`** | `Http::StreamFilter` interface that the filter implements (`decodeHeaders`, `decodeData`, `decodeTrailers`, `encodeHeaders`, etc.). |\n| **`envoy/grpc/async_client_manager.h`** | Used to create/retrieve gRPC async clients for communicating with the authorization service. |\n| **`envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`** | Used by the HTTP client to find the thread-local cluster for the authorization service. |\n| **`envoy/runtime/runtime.h`** | Runtime feature flags for `filter_enabled` (fractional percentage) and `deny_at_disable`. |\n| **`envoy/stats/scope.h`, `envoy/stats/stats_macros.h`** | Stats infrastructure for counters (`ok`, `denied`, `error`, `disabled`, `failure_mode_allowed`, `invalid`, etc.). |\n| **`envoy/stream_info/filter_state.h`** | `FilterState` used to store `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` for access logging and CEL. |\n| **`source/common/http/utility.h`** | HTTP utilities (query parameter parsing, WebSocket/H2 upgrade detection, per-filter-config resolution). |\n| **`source/common/router/config_impl.h`** | Route configuration utilities. |\n| **`source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h`** | `FactoryBase` template used by `ExtAuthzFilterConfig` for filter registration. |\n\n**Proto dependencies:**\n\n- `envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.proto` \u2014 Filter configuration (`ExtAuthz`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `CheckSettings`, `HttpService`, `BufferSettings`).\n- `envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto` \u2014 The `CheckRequest`/`CheckResponse` messages and `Authorization` service definition.\n- `envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto` \u2014 gRPC service configuration.\n- `envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto` \u2014 Header mutation rules.\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n- **Envoy HTTP Connection Manager**: The filter is instantiated as part of the HTTP filter chain. It is registered under the name `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` (legacy name: `envoy.ext_authz`) via `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY` in `config.cc:84`.\n- **Per-route configuration**: Virtual hosts, routes, and weighted clusters can customize behavior via `ExtAuthzPerRoute` (disable the filter, add context extensions, override the authorization service, override body buffering settings). The filter resolves per-route config via `Http::Utility::resolveMostSpecificPerFilterConfig<FilterConfigPerRoute>()` and merges configs from multiple levels.\n- **Access logging / CEL**: `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` is stored in `FilterState` under the filter's config name, exposing fields like `latency_us`, `bytesSent`, `bytesReceived` for use in access log formatters and CEL expressions.\n- **Dynamic metadata**: The filter writes dynamic metadata under namespace `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` that downstream filters can consume (e.g., the `ext_authz_duration` field).\n- **Network ext_authz filter**: `source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/` is a sibling TCP-level filter sharing the same common library (`filters/common/ext_authz/`).\n\n## 3. Relevant Components\n\n### Core HTTP Filter\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Main filter header. Defines:\n  - `ExtAuthzFilterStats` \u2014 counter definitions (`ok`, `denied`, `error`, `disabled`, `failure_mode_allowed`, `invalid`, `ignored_dynamic_metadata`, `filter_state_name_collision`, `omitted_response_headers`, `request_header_limits_reached`, `response_header_limits_reached`).\n  - `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` \u2014 `FilterState::Object` storing per-request latency, bytes sent/received, cluster info, upstream host, gRPC status for access logging.\n  - `FilterConfig` \u2014 immutable configuration parsed from proto (failure mode, body buffering, header mutation rules, status on error, metadata namespaces, etc.).\n  - `FilterConfigPerRoute` \u2014 per-route settings (context extensions, disable flag, body buffering override, per-route gRPC/HTTP service override).\n  - `Filter` \u2014 the `Http::StreamFilter` implementation with state machine (`NotStarted` -> `Calling` -> `Complete`).\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.cc`**: Main filter implementation. Key functions:\n  - `FilterConfig::FilterConfig()` (line 77) \u2014 parses proto configuration into C++ fields.\n  - `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (line 398) \u2014 entry point; checks per-route flags, decides whether to buffer body, initiates the check call.\n  - `Filter::decodeData()` (line 451) \u2014 handles request body buffering.\n  - `Filter::initiateCall()` (line 275) \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` via `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()`, merges per-route context extensions, handles per-route service overrides, and calls `client_->check()`.\n  - `Filter::onComplete()` (line 631) \u2014 callback handling the `CheckResponse`: OK path (mutates request headers, query params, saves response headers), Denied path (sends local reply with authz-specified status/headers/body), Error path (failure_mode_allow or reject).\n  - `Filter::onDestroy()` (line 613) \u2014 cancels in-flight requests.\n  - `Filter::encodeHeaders()` (line 489) \u2014 adds saved response headers to the upstream response on the encode path.\n  - `Filter::createPerRouteGrpcClient()` (line 208) \u2014 creates a gRPC client for per-route service overrides.\n  - `Filter::createPerRouteHttpClient()` (line 252) \u2014 creates an HTTP client for per-route service overrides.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.h`**: Filter factory (`ExtAuthzFilterConfig`). Registered as `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`.\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config.cc`**: Factory implementation. Creates either a `GrpcClientImpl` or `RawHttpClientImpl` based on configuration (line 31: `if (proto_config.has_http_service())`).\n\n### Common Library (shared with network ext_authz)\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz.h`**: Abstract `Client` interface with `check()` and `cancel()` methods. `Response` struct with `CheckStatus` (`OK`, `Denied`, `Error`), header mutations, body, status code, dynamic metadata, gRPC status. `RequestCallbacks` with `onComplete()`. Tracing constants and response code details.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl.h/.cc`**: `GrpcClientImpl` \u2014 sends unary gRPC `Check` RPC. Handles `onSuccess()` (parses `OkHttpResponse`/`DeniedHttpResponse`/`ErrorHttpResponse`, copies header mutations, dynamic metadata) and `onFailure()` (returns `CheckStatus::Error`).\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl.h/.cc`**: `RawHttpClientImpl` \u2014 sends HTTP request to the authorization cluster. `ClientConfig` manages header matchers for upstream/client/dynamic-metadata headers. `toResponse()` maps HTTP 200 to OK, 5xx to Error, everything else to Denied. Supports retry policy.\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils.h/.cc`**: `CheckRequestUtils::createHttpCheck()` \u2014 builds the `CheckRequest` proto from stream callbacks, headers, body, peer certificates, TLS session, metadata, destination labels, and header matchers.\n\n### Proto Definitions\n\n- **`api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/v3/ext_authz.proto`**: `ExtAuthz` message (main config), `HttpService`, `AuthorizationRequest`, `AuthorizationResponse`, `ExtAuthzPerRoute`, `CheckSettings`, `BufferSettings`.\n- **`api/envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto`**: `CheckRequest`, `CheckResponse`, `OkHttpResponse`, `DeniedHttpResponse`, `ErrorHttpResponse`, `Authorization` service with `Check` RPC.\n\n### Build Configuration\n\n- **`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/BUILD`**: Bazel build file listing all deps for the `ext_authz` library and `config` extension.\n\n## 4. Failure Modes\n\n### Authorization Service Unavailable\n\n- **gRPC**: `GrpcClientImpl::onFailure()` is called with a non-OK gRPC status. This produces a `Response` with `CheckStatus::Error` and the gRPC status code.\n- **HTTP**: If the cluster doesn't exist (`thread_local_cluster == nullptr`), `errorResponse()` is returned immediately. If the HTTP request fails (connection reset, buffer limit exceeded), `RawHttpClientImpl::onFailure()` returns `errorResponse()`. If the authz server returns HTTP 5xx, `toResponse()` treats it as an error.\n\n### Error Handling in the Filter (`onComplete` with `CheckStatus::Error`)\n\nThe `failure_mode_allow` configuration determines behavior (ext_authz.cc, line 1039):\n\n- **`failure_mode_allow: true`** (fail-open): The request is allowed through. The `failure_mode_allowed` counter is incremented. If `failure_mode_allow_header_add` is also true, the header `x-envoy-auth-failure-mode-allowed: true` is added to the request so upstream services know auth was skipped. A custom error response status code, headers, and body from the authorization server can also be used.\n- **`failure_mode_allow: false`** (fail-closed, the default): A local reply is sent with the configured `status_on_error` (default: HTTP 403 Forbidden) or a custom status code from the error response. The response flag `UnauthorizedExternalService` is set.\n\n### Authorization Denied\n\nWhen the authz service denies the request (ext_authz.cc, line 944):\n- The `denied` counter is incremented.\n- The response flag `UnauthorizedExternalService` is set.\n- A local reply is sent with the status code from the authz response (default: HTTP 403), the response body (optionally truncated to `max_denied_response_body_bytes`), and headers specified by the authz server.\n\n### Invalid Authorization Response\n\nWhen `validate_mutations: true` and the authz response contains invalid headers or query parameters (ext_authz.cc, line 1091):\n- The `invalid` counter is incremented.\n- A local reply with HTTP 500 is sent with response code detail `ext_authz_invalid`.\n\n### Request Body Too Large\n\nWhen `with_request_body.max_request_bytes` is set and `allow_partial_message: false`:\n- If the body exceeds the limit, Envoy returns HTTP 413 (Payload Too Large) *without* calling the authz service.\n- If `allow_partial_message: true`, the body is truncated and sent with the `x-envoy-auth-partial-body: true` header.\n\n### Filter Disabled\n\nWhen the filter is disabled (via runtime flag or per-route config):\n- If `deny_at_disable` is true, requests are rejected with `status_on_error`.\n- Otherwise, requests pass through without authorization.\n\n### Timeout\n\n- Both gRPC and HTTP clients support configurable timeouts (default: 200ms).\n- A timeout results in an error response, handled the same as service unavailability.\n\n### Header/Response Limits\n\n- `enforce_response_header_limits: true` causes the filter to send HTTP 500 if adding response headers from the authz service would exceed the header map's size or count limits.\n- `request_header_limits_reached` and `response_header_limits_reached` counters track these events.\n\n## 5. Testing\n\n### Unit Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_test.cc`**: Comprehensive unit tests for the HTTP filter. Tests cover all response paths (OK, Denied, Error), header mutation, body buffering, per-route configuration, dynamic metadata, failure modes, query parameter mutations, header validation, and edge cases. Uses mocked `Client` and `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks`.\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/config_test.cc`**: Tests for the filter factory configuration parsing.\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_impl_test.cc`**: Unit tests for the gRPC client implementation (response parsing, header copying, error handling, dynamic metadata).\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_impl_test.cc`**: Unit tests for the HTTP client implementation (request construction, response parsing, header matching, error handling, retry policy).\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/check_request_utils_test.cc`**: Tests for `CheckRequest` construction from stream attributes.\n\n### Integration Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_integration_test.cc`**: End-to-end integration tests using Envoy's integration test framework. Tests gRPC and HTTP authz services, body buffering, header manipulation, per-route overrides, and failure modes. Includes tests with both HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 downstream protocols.\n\n### Fuzz Tests\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_grpc_fuzz_test.cc`**: Fuzz testing for gRPC ext_authz.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_http_fuzz_test.cc`**: Fuzz testing for HTTP ext_authz.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz_lib.{h,cc}`**: Shared fuzz test library.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz_fuzz.proto`**: Proto for fuzz test cases.\n- Fuzz corpus directories: `ext_authz_grpc_corpus/`, `ext_authz_http_corpus/`.\n\n### Test Support Files\n\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/mocks.{h,cc}`**: Mock `Client` implementation for unit testing.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz/test_common.{h,cc}`**: Test utilities (e.g., `TestCommon::makeCheckResponse()`).\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/logging_test_filter.{cc,proto}`**: A test filter used in integration tests to verify logging info in filter state.\n- **`test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz/ext_authz.yaml`**: Example YAML configuration for tests.\n\n### Running Tests\n\nTests are built using Bazel. To run specific tests:\n\n```bash\n# Unit tests for the HTTP filter\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_test\n\n# Integration tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/http/ext_authz:ext_authz_integration_test\n\n# Common library tests\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:ext_authz_grpc_impl_test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:ext_authz_http_impl_test\nbazel test //test/extensions/filters/common/ext_authz:check_request_utils_test\n```\n\n## 6. Debugging\n\n### Logs\n\nThe filter uses Envoy's logging framework with logger ID `ext_authz`:\n\n- **Trace level** (`-l trace`): Most detailed. Logs every header mutation, check request/response details, query parameter changes, body buffering decisions.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter calling authorization server.\"` \u2014 Check call initiated.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter added header(s) to the request:\"` \u2014 Header mutations on OK response.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter rejected the request. Response status code: '{}'\"` \u2014 Denied response.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter allowed the request with error\"` \u2014 Failure mode allowed.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter is buffering the request\"` \u2014 Body buffering active.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter is truncating the response body from {} to {} bytes.\"` \u2014 Body truncation.\n\n- **Debug level**: Key decision points like buffering start/stop, route cache clearing, per-route client creation.\n  - `\"ext_authz is clearing route cache\"` \u2014 Route cache cleared after header mutation.\n  - `\"ext_authz filter: using per-route gRPC service configuration.\"` \u2014 Per-route override active.\n  - `\"ext_authz cluster '{}' does not exist\"` \u2014 HTTP client cluster missing.\n\n- **Warn level**: Used with `ENVOY_LOG_EVERY_POW_2` for response header limit violations and per-route client creation failures.\n\n- The gRPC client logs at trace level: `\"Sending CheckRequest: {}\"` and `\"Received CheckResponse: {}\"` with full proto debug strings.\n\n### Stats / Metrics\n\nAll counters are prefixed with `ext_authz.` (or `ext_authz.<stat_prefix>.` if `stat_prefix` is configured):\n\n| Counter | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `ext_authz.ok` | Requests authorized successfully |\n| `ext_authz.denied` | Requests denied by the authz service |\n| `ext_authz.error` | Errors communicating with the authz service |\n| `ext_authz.disabled` | Requests where the filter was disabled (via runtime or metadata) |\n| `ext_authz.failure_mode_allowed` | Requests allowed through despite authz errors (fail-open) |\n| `ext_authz.invalid` | Responses rejected due to invalid mutations (`validate_mutations: true`) |\n| `ext_authz.ignored_dynamic_metadata` | Dynamic metadata rejected because ingestion is disabled |\n| `ext_authz.filter_state_name_collision` | Filter state name already in use by another filter |\n| `ext_authz.omitted_response_headers` | Response headers dropped due to header map limits |\n| `ext_authz.request_header_limits_reached` | Request header mutations rejected due to limits |\n| `ext_authz.response_header_limits_reached` | Response header mutations rejected due to limits |\n\nAdditionally, if `charge_cluster_response_stats: true` (default), the filter increments cluster-scoped stats (e.g., `cluster.<cluster>.ext_authz.ok`, `cluster.<cluster>.ext_authz.denied`, etc.) and charges HTTP response code stats against the cluster for denied responses.\n\n### Traces\n\n- The gRPC client creates a child span from the parent span passed to `check()`. The span is tagged with:\n  - `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok`, `ext_authz_unauthorized`, or `ext_authz_error`.\n- The HTTP client creates a child span named `\"async <cluster> egress\"`. The span is tagged with:\n  - `ext_authz_http_status`: The HTTP status code from the authz server.\n  - `ext_authz_status`: `ext_authz_ok` or `ext_authz_unauthorized`.\n\n### Filter State (Access Logging)\n\nWhen `emit_filter_state_stats: true`, the filter writes `ExtAuthzLoggingInfo` to `FilterState` under the filter's config name. This exposes:\n\n- `latency_us` \u2014 Authorization call latency in microseconds (available for both gRPC and HTTP).\n- `bytesSent` \u2014 Bytes sent to the authz service (gRPC only).\n- `bytesReceived` \u2014 Bytes received from the authz service (gRPC only).\n- Upstream host and cluster info (gRPC only).\n- gRPC status code (gRPC only).\n\nThese can be referenced in access log format strings and CEL expressions.\n\n### Response Flags\n\nThe filter sets the `UF` (UnauthorizedExternalService) response flag on denied and error (fail-closed) responses. This appears in access logs as `UF`.\n\n### Response Code Details\n\nThe filter sets response code details that appear in access logs:\n\n- `ext_authz_denied` \u2014 Request was denied.\n- `ext_authz_error` \u2014 Authz service error (fail-closed).\n- `ext_authz_invalid` \u2014 Invalid authz response was rejected.\n\n### Dynamic Metadata\n\nOn OK responses, the filter writes dynamic metadata under `envoy.filters.http.ext_authz` including the authz service's dynamic metadata and `ext_authz_duration` (latency in milliseconds). This can be logged or used by downstream filters.\n\n### Common Debugging Workflow\n\n1. **Check stats**: Look at `ext_authz.ok`, `ext_authz.denied`, `ext_authz.error` counters to understand the distribution of responses.\n2. **Enable trace logging**: Set log level to `trace` for the `ext_authz` logger to see full request/response details.\n3. **Check response flags**: Look for `UF` in access logs to identify authz-related failures.\n4. **Check response code details**: `ext_authz_denied`, `ext_authz_error`, or `ext_authz_invalid` indicate the specific failure type.\n5. **Verify cluster health**: Ensure the authz service cluster is healthy (check `cluster.<cluster>.membership_healthy`, `cluster.<cluster>.upstream_rq_*` stats).\n6. **Check timeouts**: If `ext_authz.error` is high, check if the authz service is responding within the configured timeout (default: 200ms).\n7. **Inspect tracing**: Use distributed tracing to see the ext_authz child span, its duration, and status tags.\n8. **Filter state stats**: If `emit_filter_state_stats` is enabled, check access logs for latency and bytes metrics per request.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/onboarding.md
# ext_authz Filter Handoff Document

## 1. Purpose

The ext_authz HTTP filter (`envoy.filters.http.ext_authz`) implements external authorization for Envoy proxy. It delegates authorization decisions to an external service before allowing requests to proceed upstream.

**What it does:**

- Intercepts incoming HTTP requests and constructs an authorization check request (a `CheckRequest` protobuf) containing request attributes (headers, path, method, source/destination info, TLS details, request body, metadata).
- Sends this check request to a configured external authorization service via either **gRPC** (using the `envoy.service.auth.v3.Authorization.Check` RPC) or **raw HTTP** (by forwarding selected headers to an HTTP cluster).
- Based on the response (`OK`, `Denied`, or `Error`), the filter either allows the request to continue upstream (potentially mutating headers/query parameters), returns a denial response to the client, or handles the error according to its `failure_mode_allow` configuration.

**When to use it:**

- When authorization logic needs to live outside Envoy (e.g., a centralized policy engine like OPA, a custom auth service, or a third-party authorization provider).
- When you need to enforce access control policies that require context beyond what Envoy natively evaluates (e.g., checking JWTs against a user database, enforcing RBAC policies, rate limiting based on user identity).
- When different routes/virtual hosts need different authorization behavior (via per-route configuration).

There is also a **network-level** variant (`envoy.filters.network.ext_authz`) at `source/extensions/filters/network/ext_authz/` that operates at the TCP layer, but this document focuses on the HTTP filter.
